<p><b>PJSC Sberbank</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru"><b>Сбербанк</b></span>, initially a contraction of "<i>сберегательный банк</i>" – sberegatelnyy bank; English: "<a href="/wiki/Savings_bank" title="Savings bank">savings bank</a>") is a state-owned Russian banking and <a href="/wiki/Financial_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial service">financial services</a> company headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>. The company was known as "Sberbank of Russia" until 2015. Sberbank has operations in several European and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">post-Soviet countries</a>. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> it was the largest bank in Russia and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, and the third largest in Europe, ranked <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_banks" title="List of largest banks">33rd in the world</a> and first in central and Eastern Europe in <a href="/wiki/The_Banker" title="The Banker">The Banker</a>'s Top 1000 World Banks ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Banker_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Banker-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_12_November_2001-7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Putin</a> visits a <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> branch of Sberbank, November 2001</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RR5115-0027R.gif" class="image"><img alt="Russian 25 rubles coin" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/RR5115-0027R.gif/220px-RR5115-0027R.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/03/RR5115-0027R.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RR5115-0027R.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian coin commemorating the establishment of the first savings banks in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in 1841.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sberbank's history goes back to <a href="/wiki/Georg_von_Cancrin" class="mw-redirect" title="Georg von Cancrin">Cancrin</a>'s financial reform of 1841,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> when a network of the first state-owned savings banks was created in Russia. By the end of the 19th century, the network reached almost 4 thousand outlets with over 2 million depositors.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1905, savings bank outlets became authorised to sell insurance. After 1910, savings banks started subsidising credit cooperation institutions and extending loans to small lenders. In 1915, savings bank outlets started accepting government securities for depositing.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_savings_banks_system">Soviet savings banks system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Soviet savings banks system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> of 1917, the state savings banks system continued its activity and growth under the management of the Finance Ministry of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a> as the State Labour Savings Banks System. From 1926, the saving bank outlets were used to pay wages to blue- and white-collar workers. The savings banks were used to distribute state lottery tickets and for the placement of state bonds with the population. The savings banks introduced wider services such as money transfers.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By late 1980s, the Soviet savings bank system had almost 80 thousand branches. As part of <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">Perestroika</a> reforms, in 1987 the savings bank outlets are reorganised into the Savings Bank of the USSR. Within the Savings bank of the USSR,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> separate savings banks were created in the Soviet Republics. Following the dissolution of the USSR, the former republican savings banks became state savings banks of the newly independent post-Soviet states.
</p><p>In 1991, the Savings bank of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">RSFSR</a> has been reorganised into the Joint-Stock Commercial Savings Bank of the Russian Federation (Sberbank of Russia).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sberbank_of_Russia">Sberbank of Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Sberbank of Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In post-Soviet Russia, Sberbank is the largest universal bank despite growing competition from private and other state-owned commercial banks. The bank has gradually expanded its international presence.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2007, Sberbank is led by former economy minister Herman Gref.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Volksbank_International_acquisition.2C_2011"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Volksbank_International_acquisition,_2011">Volksbank International acquisition, 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Volksbank International acquisition, 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, Sberbank acquired <a href="/wiki/Volksbank" title="Volksbank">Volksbank International AG</a> from its shareholders <a href="/wiki/Volksbank" title="Volksbank">Österreichische Volksbanken AG</a>, <a href="/wiki/BPCE" class="mw-redirect" title="BPCE">BPCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/DZ_Bank" title="DZ Bank">DZ Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/WGZ_Bank" title="WGZ Bank">WGZ Bank</a>. The deal included all VBI assets - banks in <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, except for Volksbank <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>. The agreed price was €585 to €645 million, depending on VBI business performance in 2011. VBI's total assets excluding Romania was €9.4 billion in June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> On 16 December 2013, Volksbank (Ukraine), which was a wholly owned subsidiary of Sberbank, changed its name to «<a href="https://uk.wikipedia.org/wiki/VS_Bank" class="extiw" title="uk:VS Bank">VS Bank</a>» (Ukrainian: ВіЕс Банк).<sup id="cite_ref-VSBank_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VSBank-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Denizbank_acquisition.2C_2012"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Denizbank_acquisition,_2012">Denizbank acquisition, 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Denizbank acquisition, 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2012 Sberbank bought the Turkish <a href="/wiki/DenizBank" title="DenizBank">DenizBank</a> for <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Lira" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Lira">Turkish Lira</a> 6,469 billion (about EUR 2,821 billion or US$3.504 billion) from the lender <a href="/wiki/Dexia" title="Dexia">Dexia</a>, which in 2011 was "partly nationalized by the governments of France, Belgium and Luxembourg".<sup id="cite_ref-nyt2012_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt2012-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The deal included DenizBank subsidiaries in Turkey, Austria and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="US.2C_EU.2C_Switzerland.2C_and_Ukraine_sanctions:_2014-2017"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="US,_EU,_Switzerland,_and_Ukraine_sanctions:_2014-2017">US, EU, Switzerland, and Ukraine sanctions: 2014-2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: US, EU, Switzerland, and Ukraine sanctions: 2014-2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of the Crimean Peninsula</a> by Russia in 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Obama_administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Obama administration">Obama administration</a> imposed sanctions on 12 September 2014, through the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Treasury" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Treasury">US Department of Treasury</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Foreign_Assets_Control" title="Office of Foreign Assets Control">Office of Foreign Assets Control</a> (OFAC) by adding Sberbank and other entities to the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Foreign_Assets_Control#Specially_Designated_Nationals_List" title="Office of Foreign Assets Control">Specially Designated Nationals List (SDN)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-treasury.gov_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treasury.gov-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SDNlist_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDNlist-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sanctions_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanctions-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ukraine-EO13660_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ukraine-EO13660-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ukraine-EO13661_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ukraine-EO13661-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ukraine-EO13662_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ukraine-EO13662-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> This was done in concert with 31 July 2014 addition of Sberbank to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_individuals_sanctioned_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="List of individuals sanctioned during the Ukrainian crisis">European Union sanctions list</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters2014_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters2014-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Sanctions consist of access restriction to the EU and US capital markets.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> After announcement of the sanctions, and by the end of July, Sberbank's market value had dropped the most market value among the world's major lenders plus investors moved $22 billion from Sberbank's market capitalization.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Still, during the following year Sberbank's share price grew back 89%.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Sberbank together with other Russian banks filed claims with the highest EU court to lift the punitive economic measures.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 August 2014, Switzerland imposed sanctions on Sberbank and other Russian financial institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-SwissSanctions_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SwissSanctions-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 December 2015, the United States imposed additional sanctions on Sberbank and its subsidiaries.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-treasury.gov_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treasury.gov-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SDNlist_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDNlist-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ukraine-EO13662_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ukraine-EO13662-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 October 2016, Ukraine imposed sanctions against Sberbank Russia, Sberbank Leasing, and their payment systems Kolibri (Hummingbird), formerly Blitz (Ukrainian: «Колибри» стара назва – «Блиц»).<sup id="cite_ref-MailSanctions_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MailSanctions-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-467Ukraine2016_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-467Ukraine2016-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Annex4_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annex4-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 March 2017, the president of Ukraine imposed sanctions on Sberbank (and other Russian state-owned banks operating in Ukraine: VTB Bank, BM Bank, Prominvestbank, and <a href="https://uk.wikipedia.org/wiki/VS_Bank" class="extiw" title="uk:VS Bank">VS Bank</a> (Ukrainian: ВіЕс Банк)) as part of its continued sanctions on Russia for its <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a> and involvement in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">War in Donbass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SBoUnsf_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBoUnsf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63Ukraine2017_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63Ukraine2017-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-March16Ukraine2017sanctionsBanks_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-March16Ukraine2017sanctionsBanks-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_sale_of_VS_Bank_to_Tihipko">2017 sale of VS Bank to Tihipko</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2017 sale of VS Bank to Tihipko">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2017, due to sanctions, Sberbank sold its Ukrainian subsidiary, "VS Bank" (Ukrainian: ВіЕс Банк)<sup id="cite_ref-SBoUnsf_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBoUnsf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> to Ukrainian businessman <a href="/wiki/Serhiy_Tihipko" title="Serhiy Tihipko">Serhiy Tihipko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNIANTihipkoBuysVS_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIANTihipkoBuysVS-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The majority shareholder of Sberbank is the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Bank of the Russian Federation">Central Bank of the Russian Federation</a>, owning 50%+1 voting share of Sberbank's voting shares. The rest of the shares are dispersed among portfolio, private and other investors with an estimated shareholding of over 43% held by foreigners.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Russia's central bank cannot sell its stake without a change in Russia's laws.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The President and <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Executive Officer">Chief Executive Officer</a> is <a href="/wiki/German_Gref" class="mw-redirect" title="German Gref">Herman Gref</a>, confirmed by the Board of Directors on 16 October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sergei_Gorkov" title="Sergei Gorkov">Sergei Gorkov</a> joined Sberbank in November 2008 eventually becoming the head of the international operations and the Senior Vice Chairman of the Board from 10 October 2010, until 26 February 2016, when he left Sberbank to become the Chairman of <a href="/wiki/Vnesheconombank" class="mw-redirect" title="Vnesheconombank">Vnesheconombank</a> (VEB).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TASS26-02-2016_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TASS26-02-2016-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He greatly expanded Sberbank from operations in only two foreign countries, Kazakhstan (2006)<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KazakhstanSberbank_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KazakhstanSberbank-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and Ukraine (December 2007),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UkraineSberbank_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UkraineSberbank-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> to over twenty countries including Belarus (2009),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BelarusSberbank_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BelarusSberbank-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Germany (2009),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GermanySberbank_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GermanySberbank-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> China (2010),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChinaSberbank_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaSberbank-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> India (September 2010),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IndiaSberbank_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiaSberbank-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Switzerland (31 December 2011),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SwitzerlandBloomberg_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SwitzerlandBloomberg-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Austria (acquisition of Volksbank International AG on 15 February 2012; changed name to Sberbank Europe AG on 1 November 2012, with locations in Austria, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Croatia, Czech Republic, Hungary, Slovakia, Slovenia, Serbia, Ukraine, and Germany),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AustriaBloomberg_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AustriaBloomberg-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Bosnia-Herzegovina (20 February 2013),<sup id="cite_ref-BosniaBloomberg_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BosniaBloomberg-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Hungary (31 December 2011; 1 November 2013, as Sberbank Hungary Ltd),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HungaryBloomberg_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryBloomberg-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Croatia (February 2012),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CroatiaBloomberg_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CroatiaBloomberg-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Czech Republic (20 February 2013),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CzechBloomberg_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CzechBloomberg-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Slovenia (28 January 2013),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Serbia (24 December 2012),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SerbiaBloomberg_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SerbiaBloomberg-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Slovakia (15 February 2013),<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SlovakiaBloomberg_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SlovakiaBloomberg-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and Turkey (acquisition of DenizBank in September 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-HistorySberbank_56-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistorySberbank-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SberbankBloomberg_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SberbankBloomberg-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Following Gorkov's departure, Svetlana Alekseyevna Sagaydak (Russian: Светлана Алексеевна Cагайдак) became the new Senior Vice Chairman of the Board.<sup id="cite_ref-TASS26-02-2016_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TASS26-02-2016-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Chairman of the Supervisory Board of Sberbank is <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Mikhaylovich_Ignatyev" title="Sergey Mikhaylovich Ignatyev">Sergey Ignatiev</a>, former Chairman of the Central Bank of the Russian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Formerly from 2003 to 2013 the head of <a href="/wiki/RIA_Novosti" title="RIA Novosti">RIA Novosti</a> and from 2006 to 2016 its editor in chief, <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Mironyuk" title="Svetlana Mironyuk">Svetlana Mironyuk</a> is a vice-president and the head of marketing and communications since 1 February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 2015 the bank had about 16,500 offices with over 250,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-Sberbank_–_About_Us_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sberbank_–_About_Us-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> According to own estimates, the bank had over 137 million retail clients and over 1.1 million corporate clients in its 22 countries of presence.
</p><p>As of August 2015 it accounted for 28.6% of aggregate banking assets, calling itself "the circulatory system of the Russian economy","key lender to the Russian economy and the biggest receiver of deposits".<sup id="cite_ref-Sberbank_–_About_Us_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sberbank_–_About_Us-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Within Russia, Sberbank is structured into several regional divisions (territorial banks):
</p>

<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/45px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>
</td>
<td>Sberbank CIB
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Presentation of ice climbing in the Olympic Park of Sochi at the 2014 Winter Olympics, sponsored by Sberbank" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg/220px-IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg/330px-IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg/440px-IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IceClimbingDemonstration_at_the_Winter_Olympics_Sochi2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Presentation of ice climbing in the Olympic Park of <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>, sponsored by Sberbank</div></div></div>
<p>Sberbank sponsors sports and charity events in various regions of Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> as well as educational projects<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> including projects developing financial literacy.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Not_returning_of_citizens.27_deposits_during_privatisation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Not_returning_of_citizens'_deposits_during_privatisation">Not returning of citizens' deposits during privatisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Not returning of citizens&#039; deposits during privatisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sberbank is the successor of Soviet saving banks, whose assets belonged to the state.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Economic history of the Russian Federation">Russia's transition to a market economy in the 1990s</a>, in which these assets were sold, Sberbank provided no guarantee for citizens' deposits.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in a landslide depreciation, which in turn led to severe discontent among the Russian population.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Since 1996, partial compensation for investors' losses has been offered.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> However, until 2003 this only applied to state-owned banks such as Sberbank, giving them an <a href="/wiki/Competitive_advantage" title="Competitive advantage">unfair advantage</a> over fully private banks.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Low_level_of_service">Low level of service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Low level of service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2000s, Sberbank was repeatedly blamed for poor service.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, in subsequent years, Sberbank has introduced new services<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and improved the quality of some of its existing ones. By the mid-2010s, the bank was reportedly among the market leaders with regards to quality of client services, such as services for retail depositors,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> premium services<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and several others.
</p>
<h3><span id="Laundering_stolen_money.2C_Prevezon_Holdings.2C_and_Sergey_P._Poymanov"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Laundering_stolen_money,_Prevezon_Holdings,_and_Sergey_P._Poymanov">Laundering stolen money, Prevezon Holdings, and Sergey P. Poymanov</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Laundering stolen money, Prevezon Holdings, and Sergey P. Poymanov">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sergei_L._Magnitsky" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergei L. Magnitsky">Sergei Leonidovich Magnitsky</a> accused numerous persons and entities of laundering stolen money in tax fraud in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2017-8-2_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2017-8-2-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Owned by <a href="/wiki/Denis_Katsyv" title="Denis Katsyv">Denis Katsyv</a>, Prevezon Holdings, represented by <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Veselnitskaya" title="Natalia Veselnitskaya">Natalia Vladimirovna Veselnitskaya</a>, paid $6 million to resolve the claim without admitting any crime which subsequently led to all charges being dropped by the Justice Department in the summer of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2017-8-2_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2017-8-2-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In United States court, Sergey P. Poymanov sued Sberbank, several of its subsidiaries and executives, and a business rival for $750 million, claiming that a valuable gravel quarry he owned was illegally bankrupted and seized by the bank in a corporate raid in 2012. Sberbank says it took the quarry as collateral after Mr. Poymanov failed to repay a loan. Sberbank is retaining <a href="/wiki/Marc_Kasowitz" title="Marc Kasowitz">Marc Kasowitz</a> for this court case.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2017-8-2_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2017-8-2-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Poymanov was subsequently arrested by Russian police who then subjected him to harsh pretrial detention at a notoriously rough Moscow jail, <a href="/wiki/Matrosskaya_Tishina" title="Matrosskaya Tishina">Matrosskaya Tishina</a>, which is the same jail where Magnitsky died.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2017-8-2_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2017-8-2-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukrainian_sanctions_and_vandalism_of_Sberbank_property">Ukrainian sanctions and vandalism of Sberbank property</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ukrainian sanctions and vandalism of Sberbank property">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg/220px-Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg/330px-Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg/440px-Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boycott_Russian_bank.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">Graffiti</a> "It's a Russian bank" near the department of bank in <a href="/wiki/Oleksandriia,_Kirovohrad_Oblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Oleksandriia, Kirovohrad Oblast">Oleksandriia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a></div></div></div>
<p>In April 2014, several Ukrainian officials accused Sberbank of funding the <a href="/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine" title="2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine</a>, including alleged terrorism. The bank denied any involvement in the financing of illegal activities on Ukrainian territory, which was later confirmed by an examination carried out by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Ukraine" title="National Bank of Ukraine">National Bank of Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"It is another instance of aggressive nationalism of <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Nazi">neo-Nazi</a> dogma that is gathering momentum in Ukraine and obviously enjoys support of official authorities of the country," the Russian foreign ministry stated.<sup id="cite_ref-Talant20-02-2018_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talant20-02-2018-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> "It seems to be no coincident that the attack on the Russian Center for Science and Culture was stages immediately after Ukrainian President <a href="/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko" title="Petro Poroshenko">Petro Poroshenko</a>'s odious speech at the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Security_Conference" title="Munich Security Conference">Munich Security Conference</a>, which was overfilled with anti-Russian pronouncements and openly called fight against the Russian flag across the globe," "Ukraine’s deliberate choice to be one of only two world nations voting against the United Nations General Assembly resolution against glorification of Nazism, neo-Nazism and other discriminatory practices demonstrate which side the current Kiev regime has chosen." the Russian ministry said.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>15 March 2017, the president of Ukraine imposed sanctions on Sberbank (and other Russian state-owned banks operating in Ukraine: VTB Bank, BM Bank, Prominvestbank, and «<a href="https://uk.wikipedia.org/wiki/VS_Bank" class="extiw" title="uk:VS Bank">VS Bank</a>» (Ukrainian: ВіЕс Банк)) as part of its continued sanctions on Russia for its <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a> and involvement in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">War in Donbass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SBoUnsf_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBoUnsf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63Ukraine2017_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63Ukraine2017-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-March16Ukraine2017sanctionsBanks_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-March16Ukraine2017sanctionsBanks-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Sberbank's Ukrainian subsidiary, «VS Bank» (Ukrainian: ВіЕс Банк), has been put on sale.<sup id="cite_ref-SBoUnsf_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBoUnsf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> But as of August&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> it has been unsuccessfully trying to sell the asset after the National Bank of Ukraine blocked the sale of the bank due to a "failure to provide the necessary and sufficient documents to carry out checks on the investors in compliance with Ukrainian law."<sup id="cite_ref-SBoUnsf_43-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBoUnsf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 Sberbank was reported to be waiting for approval from the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Ukraine" title="National Bank of Ukraine">National Bank of Ukraine</a> to sell its Ukrainian subsidiaries. "Everything is prepared on our side. The question is whether we will be given a permission to sell or not by Ukrainian authorities," <a href="/wiki/Herman_Gref" title="Herman Gref">Herman Gref</a> who is the chairman of Sberbank said on the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> held in Davos in January 2018. On 13 December 2017, Sberbank sold another subsidiary, «VS Bank» (Ukrainian: ВіЕс Банк), to a Ukrainian banker, former <a href="/wiki/PrivatBank" title="PrivatBank">PrivatBank</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Sergiy_Tigipko" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergiy Tigipko">Sergiy Tigipko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNIANTihipkoBuysVS_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIANTihipkoBuysVS-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Talant20-02-2018_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talant20-02-2018-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Troika_Laundromat">Troika Laundromat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sberbank_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Troika Laundromat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sberbank_CIB#Troika_Laundromat" title="Sberbank CIB">Sberbank CIB §&#160;Troika Laundromat</a></div>
<p>In March 2019, the <b>Troika Laundromat</b> was exposed as an international money laundering network involving the <b>Troika Dialog</b> which is an investment bank that has been merged with the Sberbank's subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Sberbank_CIB" title="Sberbank CIB">Sberbank CIB</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OCCRPTriokaLaundromat_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCCRPTriokaLaundromat-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BNEintellinews_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNEintellinews-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RFEtroikaLaundomat_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFEtroikaLaundomat-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
